cause they are morally guilty, as well as
merely for the reason of their legal crime.
The State was never so helped before,
though the assistance came only as the legiti-
mate and impartial inquiries of a man sworn
to his duty and governed by his oath.
He was quite unprejudiced. Twice he
brought out answers favorable to the pris-
oner, even though he destroyed the effect by
the questions asked of the next witness.
And through it all he was the same dis-
passionate, judicial, evenly-balanced man
doing his duty, without fear or fayor, and
waking up the inferior minds of his 11 pup-
pets, while always sure of his own.
Antiochus began to remember the facts he
had tried to forget—an awakened public, an
angry State disgusted at its numberless
failures to convict. He felt no remorse for
the crime which had become habit, but he
began to fear the law would make a scape-
goat of him, if a jury would convict. And
he felt that conviction lay with this calm
foreman, that he was prosecutor, judge and
executioner—Outraged Morality in person
come to help Tardy Law.
He tri'Hl to catch the eye of Henry Strange
and to i -ead for pity with a glance, but could
not. The foreman did not seem to know
him but as a name. He never glanced to-
wards the dock, and apparently knew only
that its four palisades of steel held a pris-
oner.
Then Antiochus saw in this avoidance of
his glance that the foreman knew him. He
looked again and long at Henry Strange,
and tried with all his heart and soul co
remember—-yet could not. No memory
of the quiet lawyer with the pointed black
beard came to help him —no thought of one
of his many victims who had been that law-
yer’s wife. Even the judicial utterance, the
quietly used knowledge of the forms of law,
the questions that were never against the
law of evidence—these struck no answering
chord.
A laborer asking for recognition as a
prince—a clown demanding consideration as
a prophet—these are propositions to be
laughed at as he would have laughed at the
suggestion of a Judge masquerading as a
juryman. And even the suggestion never
cane to Antiochus. He could only wonder
dullv who this man was who seemed to
know his self-protective methods so well.
He scarcely heard the Judge’s summing-
up—a summing-up terribly adverse; he felt
only the presence of the real judge and the
real accuser, who was Henry Strange, iron-
moulder.
In the jury room the retirement was pro-
tracted. The foreman found two for an
acquittal and three undecided ; and he wisely
allowed the two to talk themselves out.
The view of the three undecided ones was
that many other and unarrested doctors were
equally guilty, and that Antiochus was
about to suffer for the crime of other men.
The foreman destroyed that argument with
a sentence.
“We are trying him for his own crime,”
he said. “And the evidence is beyond doubt.”
The two for acquittal had the easy moral-
ity that regards the common as the sanc-
tioned. They forgot the motive of gain, and
spoke of the kindness of the mal-practi-
tioner to women in trouble.
And then the foreman spoke leisurely, dis-
passionately, summing-up against the pris-
oner in a way that excluded argument or
denial.
“Here is a man,” he said, “who has been
twice tried for similar crimes, and has twice
escaped. He has grown rich by murder. It
was no murder of passion or intoxication;
but a calmly made and systematic plan for
gain to chance killing, while taking such
precautions in the acceptance of payment as
to make conviction almost impossible. You
will think of the disgrace of this trial; if he
is acquitted, it becomes a diploma. You
will consider him punished by the exposure
of the accusation; if it fails, it becomes an
advertisement.
“Most of us have wives and daughters.
Our ancestors made laws to protect them,
ami we assail our ancestors’ wisdom with
timidity and maladministration of the law.
Murder is not the less murder because it
takes such a form as to be almost respect-
able ; by softness to it we pave the way to
make murder more easy of commission and
more difficult of punishment. By agreeing
to regard this sort of crime easily, while the
slaying of a man by a man would fill you
with horror, you buttress the convention
that regards the foundling hospital as a pre-
mium to immorality—that despises the good
girl who keeps her love-child and works for
it, and drives the more weakly-sensitive
woman to poison or the river.”
He paused, but they were silent, and when
he proceeded, there was another presence in
the room —a presence that acted on the
waverers as a Thirteenth Juror.
“I knew one case—one of the many that
are never heard of, for a certificate of death
covers any crime. A couple happily married ;
the man devoted to his work, and so devoted
to his wife that he weakened her by keep-
ing her from the touch of the world that
makes us strong by struggling. From being
a merely happy, careless girl she became a
frivolous society woman, hating responsi-
bility. Petted and coddled as she was, had
she been a man she must have been a loafer;
being a woman, she did nothing at all but
pretend to amuse herself. She had one child,
and even that responsibility grew irksome;
she avoided motherhood; she found a scoun-
drel who, for gain, helped her avoidance.
And, gentleman, she paid the penalty. She
died.”
They were all hushed now, tensely quiet,
seeing the ghost of murder in the room—the
spirit of the woman dead before her time;
hearing the rustle of cerements and the
shroud.
“Some of you may know of such a case,”
continued Henry Strange, and they answered
him: —
“I do!”
“So do I!”
“And I do, too!”
“Then here is duty. There is no moral
doubt of the prisoner’s guilt, and no legal
doubt that can be considered. The dead ask
for our pitiless and dispassionate verdict;
the living expect protection by this verdict;
the State demands it. For ourselves, we are
sworn to do our duty without fear, favor
or affection ; and I say ‘Guilty.’ ”
Twelve jurymen brought the verdict. The
Thirteenth Juror did not accompany them,
but her vote went with them into court.
“Gentlemen of the jury—have you consid-
ered your verdict?”
“We have,” said Henry Strange.
“And what do you find?”
“We find the prisoner guilty of wilful
murder.”
“Without recommendation?”
“Without recommendation.”
The Judge put on the black cap. But the
prisoner neither looked at him nor listened
to sentence pronounced without hope of re-
prieve. He knew already. When the jury
entered, he had looked at the foreman and
i-ead Doom in his eyes.
* * * *
“The finest jury on earth,” said the State
Prosecutor. “But why not? You don’t find
a foreman like that once in a century.”
“A fine legal mind lost to the Bench,” said
his Honor.
In Westralia that day a pocket Hei’cules
of a man, who swung 141 b. hammers on in-
candescent metal as if he liked the exercise,
negotiated for a partnership in a small iron
and brass foundry. He had been paid £2OO,
and his name was Henry Strange.
In his cottage at Black Rock Mr. Justice
Harron, much more youthful looking by
reason of his clean-shaven face and almost
happy—though his eyes shone with tears —
knelt before the photograph of a woman
whose glance appealed no longer, but seemed
to praise.
“Have I done well? Are you satisfied
now?” he asked, as one expecting no reply,
of the portrait of the Thirteenth Juror.
And the man who was the pitcher that
had gone to the well once too often, won-
dered vainly for the identity of the man who
had spun his rope, trembled in the condemned
cell and shuddered for the end.

Recitative. —A Woman Who Did.
LOVE’S delight and lover’s folly
Bring me now to melancholy;
Sorrowfully, I move forsaken —
By pursuing Time o’ertaken;
Now the future darkens o’er me- —
Rough and hard the path before me.
Yet across the warp of sadness
Gleams a golden thread of gladness!
I but follow many another....
Not a wife, and yet a mother —
Ah !.... my child.... must I bemoan thee ?
Will the grudging world disown thee?
Innocent, bright flower of Passion,
Canst thou come in dubious fashion?.. ..
Never ! Let the scorners mock ,thee,
So I can but feed and frock thee.
I care nothing !.. . . oh, what made me ?.. . .
Surely—surely some will aid me !... .
Chorus of Federal Ministers: —
How blessed are the merciful! How worthy
are the meek!
How merry are the generous who others’
welfare seek!
The poor in heart are far, far worse than
poor in pocket are,
And meanness is a greater curse than shoddy
or “Three Star!”
We’ve tried to do a little good—we hope to
do a lot!
For some of our proposals we are catching
it red-hot!
But let’s be Liir—and do and dare —and let
the poop!- .-judge.
And, hr, i iif) once made up our minds, refuse
io bend or budge!
We've brought a little Bunus in—a helpful
kind of Bill
Intended to assist the poor, and empty
cradles fill;
And if, perchance, some Little Strangers
don’t come through the Ring,
They’ll need the more the useful aid our little
Bill will bring!
Antipiional Chorus of Prelates, Wow-
sers and Doctors of Divinity:—
Shame ! Shame ! Shame !
Here’s a baby without any name!
How dare it arrive?
Does the Devil contrive it, or is it the
Lord we must blame?
Sin ! Sin ! Sin !
The mother looks weary and thin —
What! Give her & fiver,
And help to revive her? —If so, let the
Judgment begin!
What? What? What?
Will you subsidise Sin in a cot?
Such conduct besmirches'
The Six Hundred Churches —we tell you
to stop on the spot!
Why? Why? Why?
Do you know where you’ll go when you
die?
Do you know we shall damn you,
And into Hell ram you for bursting our
grand Marriage Tie!
Oh! Oh! Oh!
Prepare for tornadoes of Woe!
Look out for our curses,
And horrid reverses, until to your
hearses you go!
Chorus of Federal Ministers: —
Come ! Come ! Your attitude is quite
unreasonable —
We’re not proposing anything that’s
treasonable;
We’re imitating—think this no pro-
fanity—
The Founder of our common Christi-
anity !
Antiphonal Chorus: —
Your conduct is most shocking!
It’s suspiciously like mocking;
If you gave the churches cash, some
good they’d say for you !
But you’re wasting it on mothers—
Therefore know, O wicked brothers,
That, henceforth, Six Hundred Churches
cannot pray for you!
{Exeunt, singing: “Shame! Shame!
Shame!”)
Chorus of Federal Ministers:—
See, with sureness and with clarity,
What the Churches misname Charity!
On earth peasoup, cells and hominy—
Gloria, gloria tibi Domine!
N.S.W.
